Mann, holder of the Ronald L. Skaggs, FAIA Professorship in Health Facilities Design.\n\nFor additional details on the lecture series, contact Judy Pruitt at 979.845.7009 or jpruitt@tamu.edu.\n\nSee complete lecture schedule online at\n\nhttp://one.arch.tamu.edu/news/2013/8/23/lecture-integrated-project-delivery/", "icon": "https://fbstatic-a.akamaihd.net/rsrc.php/v2/yD/r/aS8ecmYRys0.gif", "type": "link", "id": "129648553793305_497140900377400", "description": "The Fall 2013 Architecture-for-Health Lecture Series will feature 13 presentations by luminaries from the design and construction industries focused on integrated project delivery \u2014 a collaborative design and construction process \u2014 as it relates to the building of modern health care facilities."}

{"from": {"id": "743619431", "name": "Michael Rollins"}, "privacy": {"value": ""}, "actions": [{"link": "https://www.facebook.com/129648553793305/posts/236989719725854", "name": "Like"}], "updated_time": "2012-02-20T19:12:37+0000", "to": {"data": [{"name": "AIAS TAMU", "id": "129648553793305"}]}, "created_time": "2012-02-20T19:12:37+0000", "message": "Second lecture of the Spring semester::\nMonday, Feb 20, 5.30p, Geren Auditorium\nRick Lowe, founder of Project Row Houses.\n\nProject Row Houses (PRH) is a neighborhood-based nonprofit art and cultural organization in Houston\u2019s Northern Third Ward, one of the city\u2019s oldest African-American communities. http://projectrowhouses.org/\n...\nDon't forget to bring your signed desk drops to the lecture for the change to win an Azimuth gift card! The winner will be posted on the archTALKS facebook page: http://www.facebook.com/archTALKS\n\nPRH began in 1993 as a result of discussions among African-American artists who wanted to establish a positive, creative presence in their own community. Artist and community activist Rick Lowe spearheaded the pursuit of this vision when he discovered the abandoned 1 1/2 block site of twenty-two shotgun-style houses in Houston\u2019s Third Ward. The shotgun houses became the perfect opportunity to pursue the creation of a new form of art. They had two key elements: 1) a beautiful form recognized by the renowned Houston artist Dr. John Biggers to be filled with architectural, spiritual, and social significance, and 2) a need for social action among the community to bring the project to life.PRH is founded on the principle that art-and the community it creates-can be the foundation for revitalizing depressed inner-city neighborhoods. This principle was is in part based on the philosophy of German artist Joseph Beuys (1921 \u2013 1986) who coined the phrase \u201csocial sculpture,\u201d which transformed the idea of sculpture as an art form into a social activity. Thus, the mission of Project Row Houses is to create community through the celebration of art, African American history and culture.", "type": "status", "id": "129648553793305_236989719725854"}

{"from": {"id": "1170324524", "name": "Brian Sowell"}, "privacy": {"value": ""}, "actions": [{"link": "https://www.facebook.com/129648553793305/posts/178444435580383", "name": "Like"}], "updated_time": "2011-11-16T00:28:03+0000", "to": {"data": [{"name": "AIAS TAMU", "id": "129648553793305"}]}, "likes": {"paging": {"cursors": {"after": "MTUyNzA2MDAwNw==", "before": "MTUyNzA2MDAwNw=="}}, "data": [{"id": "1527060007", "name": "Jake Vinson"}]}, "created_time": "2011-11-16T00:28:03+0000", "message": "Public Service Announcement for Laser Cutter Users:\nHi everyone! As many of you know I work in the woodshop and have cut many of your projects. Jim told us today that with finals upon us we must be strict with the laser cutter rules and guidelines to allow everyone equal opportunity to use the cutter and prevent any time wasted. To wit, here are the rules that you must follow if you wish to cut in the laser cutter. If you do not follow these rules, Jim has required we must turn you away and make you come back with it fixed.\n\n1. We will be closing at 5 PM, no exceptions. If you arrive with a file after 4:30 we will probably turn you away. If we do cut it and it does not finish by 5:00 we WILL end the cut and you will need to return in the morning. Come early, don't push the closing time!\n\n2. You MUST place your file on the laser cutter template. The template can be found here: http://www.arch.tamu.edu/inside/services/woodshop/ If you can't download the file or it's not working for some reason, don't bring it to us - we don't know what's wrong with your computer, and we don't have time to fix it. Please ask a friend who has been able to laser cut for their help.\n\nWhile you're there downloading the template, go ahead and read the instructions on how to use the laser cutter, as much of what I'm saying here is repeated there.\n\n3. You must have all your lines on the proper layer - the laser cutter template layer. DO NOT JUST CHANGE THE COLOR! While this will technically work, it can cause issues if you have not exploded your lines properly, and if we need to edit your drawing due to a cutting error it makes it much more difficult. Use the template, use our layers.\n\n4. Speaking of editing, we will not fix your file for you and can not allow you to edit your file on our computers. If your file has issues, we must return your file and you will need to fix it on your personal computer.\n\n5. If you do need to make edits to your file on your personal computer, please do not do it in the laser cutter room. That is a small room and it is intended for employees and people currently cutting. Any more than that and you get in our way and prevent us from doing our job.\n\n6. Lastly, with finals upon us we will be giving preference to individual school-related projects over personal projects or group projects. If you have a personal file please bring it in to cut at non-peak hours, and if you have a group project with an extensive number of boards, we will limit you to one machine, even if you have several people working on the project.\n\nThanks for being understanding as we approach the stressful end to our semester. I hope you all have an awesome Thanksgiving!!\n\n-Brian", "type": "status", "id": "129648553793305_178444435580383"}
